Medical lounge (G)
  You stand in a plain looking room, with bunk beds lining both sides. Green 
wool blankets line the beds with perfect hospital corners. At the end of this 
seemingly endless room are two doors leading to what you believe is some 
kind of latrine and shower area. On one wall there is a milk cooler next to a 
sign that shows a Drill Sergeant pointing to the room. Words are written 
over his head, "Milk makes for a strong soldier!". There is a Second 
Lieutenant Pixie with a red cross on her hat here.

Medical lounge (G)
  You stand in a plain looking room, with bunk beds lining both sides. Green 
wool blankets line the beds with perfect hospital corners. At the end of this 
seemingly endless room are two doors leading to what you believe is some 
kind of latrine and shower area. On one wall there is a milk cooler next to a 
sign that shows a Drill Sergeant pointing to the room. Words are written 
over his head, "Milk makes for a strong soldier!". There is a Second 
Lieutenant Pixie with a red cross on her hat here.

Boot Camp Headquarters (G)
  As you enter the Boot Camp Headquarters, you immediately notice that
the large main hall is adorned with feasting tables and fire pits
allowing the green recruits to relax after a hard days training.
A large mural on the northern wall depicts the founding members of the
Boot Camp standing before The Fallen Soldier on an ancient battlefield.
The other stone walls are decorated in the green and yellow insignia of
Boot Camp and various 'Boot Needs You' posters depicting an alluring Diva
dressed in the Boot Camp colours pointing at you.
From the arches leading out of the hall drift sounds of young recruits
being put through their paces and the smells of gunpowder and mud linger
in the air.

Boot Camp Headquarters (G)
  As you enter the Boot Camp Headquarters, you immediately notice that
the large main hall is adorned with feasting tables and fire pits
allowing the green recruits to relax after a hard days training.
A large mural on the northern wall depicts the founding members of the
Boot Camp standing before The Fallen Soldier on an ancient battlefield.
The other stone walls are decorated in the green and yellow insignia of
Boot Camp and various 'Boot Needs You' posters depicting an alluring Diva
dressed in the Boot Camp colours pointing at you.
From the arches leading out of the hall drift sounds of young recruits
being put through their paces and the smells of gunpowder and mud linger
in the air.

The Lobby of the Bonded Guildbase (G)
  For what is essentially a waiting room, this one really isn't too bad. 
It's clean, with torches casting a soft light easy on the eyes.  The wooden
walls have been painted a blue any sky would be proud to wear, so nice and
soothing.  A few tiny trees in ebony tubs occupy the corners, while
individual cushioned chairs are provided for visitors to rest after their
long journey to the Bonded Guild.  Books stand neatly on glass-topped
endtables to entertain as well.  Over it all presides a pretty receptionist
who always manages to remain polite but firm.

The Training Field

southeast, and wooden buildings have been built into tunnels in the
semi-surrounding mountain.

Boot Camp Headquarters (G)
  As you enter the Boot Camp Headquarters, you immediately notice that
the large main hall is adorned with feasting tables and fire pits
allowing the green recruits to relax after a hard days training.
A large mural on the northern wall depicts the founding members of the
Boot Camp standing before The Fallen Soldier on an ancient battlefield.
The other stone walls are decorated in the green and yellow insignia of
Boot Camp and various 'Boot Needs You' posters depicting an alluring Diva
dressed in the Boot Camp colours pointing at you.
From the arches leading out of the hall drift sounds of young recruits
being put through their paces and the smells of gunpowder and mud linger
in the air.

Boot Camp Headquarters (G)
  As you enter the Boot Camp Headquarters, you immediately notice that
the large main hall is adorned with feasting tables and fire pits
allowing the green recruits to relax after a hard days training.
A large mural on the northern wall depicts the founding members of the
Boot Camp standing before The Fallen Soldier on an ancient battlefield.
The other stone walls are decorated in the green and yellow insignia of
Boot Camp and various 'Boot Needs You' posters depicting an alluring Diva
dressed in the Boot Camp colours pointing at you.
From the arches leading out of the hall drift sounds of young recruits
being put through their paces and the smells of gunpowder and mud linger
in the air.

WHOOOOOOOOOOOOSH!
Boot Camp Headquarters (G)
  As you enter the Boot Camp Headquarters, you immediately notice that
the large main hall is adorned with feasting tables and fire pits
allowing the green recruits to relax after a hard days training.
A large mural on the northern wall depicts the founding members of the
Boot Camp standing before The Fallen Soldier on an ancient battlefield.
The other stone walls are decorated in the green and yellow insignia of
Boot Camp and various 'Boot Needs You' posters depicting an alluring Diva
dressed in the Boot Camp colours pointing at you.
From the arches leading out of the hall drift sounds of young recruits
being put through their paces and the smells of gunpowder and mud linger
in the air.

The Grand City of Aylor (G)
  You stand on the edge of the beautiful City of Aylor.
 
A bright light shines down from the heavens, pouring over you, bathing you
in its warm glow.  Everything around you seems rich and pure in color.  An
enormous, white temple stands to the north, taking up most of your view.
 
To reach the Aylorian Academy, you must travel up the large staircase that
stands just off the side of the church.  (Type 'UP' to learn how to play the
game.)
 
Below you are large piles of armor and equipment discarded by other
adventurers.

Entrance to a Forest (G) [**> PK <**]
  After traveling for what seems like an endless age, you finally come to
the edge of the vast northern plains.  At this northern edge, you discover a
forest, and a roughly cut path covered by vines which leads through it. 
Through the forest you hear the sounds of battle, best be wary of your way,
or return from whence you came.

Courtyard (G)
  It stinks.  The smell of sweat, tears and broken spirits fills the air.
The sounds of soldiers in training have gotten much louder as you step
into the courtyard. "I don't know but I've been told, it's hard to run
with the weight of gold." You see soldiers everywhere running laps on
a beaten path around the courtyard. Some less-fortunate soldiers are lined
up doing pushups in the mud. In the center of the courtyard lay a finely 
manicured lawn and the Boot clan flag. To the north you notice the bunk 
house, to the west the General's quarters. Suddenly, an officer grabs you 
by the shoulder and shouts "What are you gawking around for, future
soldier? It's time you enlisted!" And with that he points you east to 
the enlisting office.

A trail though the ferns...
  
A path leads off through the ferns to the north of Maple Lane, the soft 
green fronds gently brushing against your legs as you traverse the rough
trail. The fresh aroma of the forest invites you to breath deeply, the 
scents of the vegetation a delight to your senses. The high pitched 
chirping of cicadas sound in the distance and the occasional bright blue
ulysses butterfly flits and flutters over the giant fern fronds. A deep 
black shadow mirrors you as you head north, deliberately rustling the 
foliage to attract your attention. You know you have gone too far north 
when the shadow, in the form of a large black cat, leaps out from the 
ferns and blocks your way forward.

help colors
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Help Keywords : Colors Colours Ansi.
Help Category : Features.
Related Helps : Colorset, Rawcolors, Xterm.
Last Updated  : 2021-12-19 11:02:34.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------

Syntax:  color        - toggles current setting.
         color on/off - explicitly set color to on or off.

The 'color' command turns on/off MUD output coloring.  'ansi' is an alias
for 'color'.

The ANSI standard allows for 15 common colors that appear everywhere in
Aardwolf.  They are divided into normal and bright colors.

   @b / @B blue / bblue           @c / @C cyan / bcyan
   @r / @R red / bred             @m / @M magenta / bmagenta
   @g / @G green / bgreen         @w / @W white / bwhite
   @y / @Y yellow / byellow            @D gray (bright black)

Grey/bright black is not visible on all connections; use the 'seegray'
toggle to enable/disable seeing bright black.  There is no 'dark black'.

To use color codes in your title, communication, or whatever else you
write, prefix the color with '@' followed by the letter code.

For example, '@WColor @Gis @mCool.@w' will look like
              Color is Cool.               

It may help to END A SEGMENT OF COLORED TEXT WITH @w.  This changes 
the color of the text to low white.

To display an @ symbol, use @@.  @- may be used to display a tilde, though
the MUD no longer processes them and thus the standard tilde may be used.

Aardwolf allows you to customize your own independent color scheme for most
types of MUD output.  Type 'help colorset' to read about this feature.  The
syntax 'colorset colors' will display all 15 colors and their color codes
similar to the list above.

Aardwolf also supports xterm 256 color mode- see 'help xterm' for more
information.

Channels (discluding tells and echos) may have their color scheme returned 
to the channel's default color for all users after a color change has been 
displayed. To do this, simply use $C at the point where you would like to 
resume the channel's regular color. Note that it is difficult to actually 
display $C itself on a channel, e.g., for MUSHclient or CMUD a user can 
type $@ C. Also note that $C does not work in the note editor.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------

Room name: Before a Castle of Spiders
-- Room Desc Begin --
As you step into this section of the forest, you notice a continuous line of 
spiders all moving on the same path. It seems very odd... 
@w
Looking in the direction of the path, you notice a road that leads to a 
clearing in the forest. 
@w
In the clearing is a large castle. Examining the shape of the castle, you 
notice the pinnacles of the towers almost seem like... sharp ends of spider 
legs. Now that you think of it, the entire castle seems as if it was made to be
shaped like an enormous spider buried in the ground. It must be at least 100ft 
tall. In the front of the castle, you see a cat guarding the entrance.
@w

As you step into this section of the forest, you notice a continuous line of 
spiders all moving on the same path. It seems very odd... 

Looking in the direction of the path, you notice a road that leads to a 
clearing in the forest. 

In the clearing is a large castle. Examining the shape of the castle, you 
notice the pinnacles of the towers almost seem like... sharp ends of spider 
legs. Now that you think of it, the entire castle seems as if it was made to be
shaped like an enormous spider buried in the ground. It must be at least 100ft 
tall. In the front of the castle, you see a cat guarding the entrance.

Boot Camp Headquarters (G)
  As you enter the Boot Camp Headquarters, you immediately notice that
the large main hall is adorned with feasting tables and fire pits
allowing the green recruits to relax after a hard days training.
A large mural on the northern wall depicts the founding members of the
Boot Camp standing before The Fallen Soldier on an ancient battlefield.
The other stone walls are decorated in the green and yellow insignia of
Boot Camp and various 'Boot Needs You' posters depicting an alluring Diva
dressed in the Boot Camp colours pointing at you.
From the arches leading out of the hall drift sounds of young recruits
being put through their paces and the smells of gunpowder and mud linger
in the air.

Help Keywords : 'Miasma of Pain'.
Help Category : Attack Spell.
Related Helps : Acid Wave, Ice Cloud..
Last Updated  : 2017-08-20 17:27:35.

Syntax: cast 'miasma' <target>
Damage: acid
Spell Number: 351

This spell calls forth a cloud, or Miasma of Fog. The magical effects
of this fog cause intense and terrifying pain into any who come into
contact with it. As the Cloud is manifested directly over the
enemy, their destruction is assured, and their fate, sealed. This
cloud forms around only one opponent.

Spell available only to the Primary Class Mages.

Primary stat: Intelligence, Wisdom.
Affected by : Luck, Tier of caster.

Boot Camp Headquarters (G)
  As you enter the Boot Camp Headquarters, you immediately notice that
the large main hall is adorned with feasting tables and fire pits
allowing the green recruits to relax after a hard days training.
A large mural on the northern wall depicts the founding members of the
Boot Camp standing before The Fallen Soldier on an ancient battlefield.
The other stone walls are decorated in the green and yellow insignia of
Boot Camp and various 'Boot Needs You' posters depicting an alluring Diva
dressed in the Boot Camp colours pointing at you.
From the arches leading out of the hall drift sounds of young recruits
being put through their paces and the smells of gunpowder and mud linger
in the air.

The Grand City of Aylor (G)
  You stand on the edge of the beautiful City of Aylor.
 
A bright light shines down from the heavens, pouring over you, bathing you
in its warm glow.  Everything around you seems rich and pure in color.  An
enormous, white temple stands to the north, taking up most of your view.
 
To reach the Aylorian Academy, you must travel up the large staircase that
stands just off the side of the church.  (Type 'UP' to learn how to play the
game.)
 
Below you are large piles of armor and equipment discarded by other
adventurers.

Crumbling Field
  This field is slowly crumbling into the rushing river to the east. As you 
watch, more and more of the unprotected shoreline ripples away into the 
thunderous water. To the northwest, a small forest broods over the fields all
around it. Somewhere eastwards, a small trail collapses into what has become 
known as Kettermoor Crick: the fishy river leading into what is known as 
Mesolar's melting pot of debauchery. One may merely cross the Kettermoor to 
enter Fellchantry.

On the Crickbridge Road
  It was a dark and stormy night...

  There's a saying out in the darker parts of the country that, for a man
in the right kinds of trouble, all roads lead to Fellchantry. They say that
when "No Fear" Narlfryd, the famed Wolfen daredevil, needed a place to lay
low, he came to Fellchantry and knifed a guy over a card game. The story
goes that he wanted to use a vacation in a cell as a chance to let a bad
storm blow over. The authorities didn't give him the chance. They took one
look at that body, shook their heads, and walked the other way. Fellchantry
is just that kind of place. Around here, they're ALL dark and stormy nights,
and the residents like it that way just fine.

  To the east lies the bridge over Kettermoor Crick, the deceptively named
fast-running river that supplies Fellchantry with its ne'erending supply of
fish, trade taxes, and surly attitudes.

<MAPEND>
[ Exits: east west ]

The Bridge Over Kettermoor Crick
    The rushing waters of Kettermoor Crick flow far below this sturdy stone
bridge. In the miserable old days, the people that first settled this
godsforsaken scar of land built the bridge to access Fellchantry-- the squat,
sprawling island that sits astride the river like the biggest bully in the
schoolyard. Or so they say anyway... Really, it'd make just as much sense if
they built the bridge to give themselves something high enough to jump from.
Fellchantry isn't what you'd call a vacation spot. The water is colder
and darker than a witch's heart. The fog-- like a mourner's veil-- stretches
perpetually over the land, as if the sun just can't eat a big enough
breakfast to ever cook it off. This is where dreams go to die.

  To the west the Crickbridge Road leads away from town. To the east the city
of Fellchantry looms, looking like the saddest verse of the most dismal dirge
you've ever heard. If the word on the street is true, then the murdered smith
is somewhere inside, his body giving off the putrescent stench of a mystery.

<MAPEND>
[ Exits: east west ]

s
Fellchantry Square
  Here, filled with all manner of sights and smells, is Fellchantry Square.
In the constant hell of the Barony, this is where the honest (and you have
to be flexible on your definition here) citizens come to gossip, barter, and
conduct their necessary business. The square is a microcosm of the city; all
cramped buildings, bustling crowds, and narrow side streets. A guy could get
lost with the slightest wandering from the beaten path, and he probably
wouldn't like where he ended up. The only thing less welcoming than
Fellchantry's main streets are its back alleys.
 
  The spikes of the raised Kettermoor gate loom to the west like a dragon
waiting for a snack. From all other directions the cramped chaos of the
square presses in.

<MAPEND>

Fellchantry Square
  The southwestern portion of Fellchantry Square is most notable for being
the location of the city's shopping district, such as it is. Small
mercantile shops abound, each with signs boasting their wares. The largest
of the shops, the general store, boasts a sign reading: "Needful Things
For Sale or Trade." From the flow of traffic in and out of the shop, its
Things must be very Needful indeed.

  To the south marvelous things are for sale. To the north and east
the square offers other amusements.

The General Store
  What purports to be a simple general store on the outside is somehow so
much more on the inside... The shop's proprietor prides himself on having
something for everyone, and to that end the shop is a mess of shelves and
racks, each holding its own little universe of odds and ends. The General
Store is the sort of place where one enters and seems to find the very
thing they were just wishing they had. The deep shadows lining the far
corners of the shop, and the way the hushed whispers of customers suddenly
cease when anyone gets too close, are enough to show most just how sinister
the desires of the clientele can be. In Fellchantry everything is for sale,
and affording the price isn't always a matter of money.
  
  The front door leads north back to the square, but who could leave when
their heart's most cherished treasure is bound to be on the next shelf they
see? Stay a while... Stay a while...

<MAPEND>
[ Exits: north ]
An older gentleman in fine dress tends to the many curios in the shop.

e
Fellchantry Square
  Most of the traffic at this intersection of the square is either coming
from or going toward the south. The third most corrupt organization in the
city (after its government, and its law enforcement) has its guild hall in
that direction, and with the recent trade talks announced by the Baron there
are plenty of foreigners and citizens alike who feel the need to visit the
Merchant's Guild. Hatred and bigotry wash from Fellchantry's citizens in a
palpable wave toward the outlanders with their strange features, strange
clothing, and strange ways. Likewise in a southerly direction are the homes
of some of Fellchantry's more affluent, non-royal citizens, as well as
several other guild halls. There is even said to be an assassin's guild,
but who can afford to believe everything they hear?
   
  Affluence is to the south, along with all the dark deeds it can buy. The
press of stinking bodies in the square is all around.

<MAPEND>
[ Exits: north east south west ]
A man in a guard's uniform walks here, no doubt a justiciary.

e
Fellchantry Square
  A very curious amount of folks who traffic to the south have their hoods 
drawn, save the braver and more scary-looking individuals who stalk with the 
deadly (and frankly, sometimes swaying) grace of the land's most hardened 
criminals, traffickers and scorned illegitimate children ever to be produced
on Andolorian soil. It's not difficult to suss out the fact that in yonder 
direction lies a network of alleyways, nor is it difficult to determine that 
some folks are simply not welcome among the raff. Nay, quite often an unlucky
individual would find themselves pleading, hoisted by their britches and 
tossed from the narrow building flanks into the pounded cobble below, ejected
from the seedy underbelly of Fellchantry.

Brimtoil Alley
  The entrance to the small network of Fellchantry's alleyways seems to be more
populated than further in. Establishments, all of clean and honorable repute 
of course, have taken down walls and built doors, setting up tables or stalls
along the eastern and western side, trading in weapons, oddly valuable 
jewelry, gems, glass passed off as gems, illusions passed off as glass, and 
lies passed off as illusions. Upon close inspection, one may even spy one of 
the Justiciary among the patrons of this fine market road.

Further south, the alleyway eventually twists east and out of sight.

Brimtoil Alley
  Past the northern bustle one comes to the calmer, plainer and saner
environment of Fellchantry's alleyways. There are still the odd buildings 
with awkward doors upon surprisingly sturdy hinges from which men and women 
conduct their many creative business ventures, though they are sparser, the 
people here skinnier and rattier, their eyes sharper, and their weapons 
always at hand. A sharp curve eventually leads across a small bridge to the 
east, eventually plunging even deeper into the (known) underbelly of the 
barony.

<MAPEND>

Brimtoil Alley
  The entrance to the small network of Fellchantry's alleyways seems to be more
populated than further in. Establishments, all of clean and honorable repute 
of course, have taken down walls and built doors, setting up tables or stalls
along the eastern and western side, trading in weapons, oddly valuable 
jewelry, gems, glass passed off as gems, illusions passed off as glass, and 
lies passed off as illusions. Upon close inspection, one may even spy one of 
the Justiciary among the patrons of this fine market road.

Further south, the alleyway eventually twists east and out of sight.

<MAPEND>

Fellchantry Square (1299)

Fellchantry Square (1298)

The Heart of the Mystery
  Alas, some foul tragedy seems to have occurred here, for nothing else
could so reliably draw such a diverse crowd of onlookers. Loud cries of
"Murder most foul!" and "What villainy!" abound. At the center of the
whole mess, mayhap literally as well as figuratively, stand a group of His
Majesty's Justiciars observing one very dead body. The darkness of the
deed and the storm of intrigue sure to follow are a fitting complement to
the dark and stormy nights so common in the Barony.

  Fellchantry Square stretches out in all directions, oblivious to the
fact that Death has paid a visit nearby.

<MAPEND>

n
Fellchantry Square [**> PK <**]
    The signature smell of Fellchantry (jokingly referred to as "Kettermoor
Cologne") wafts in with particular potency from the west, hinting at
the docks to be found in that direction. The aroma, not so much unpleasant
as it is unusual, has strong fishy accents punctuated with less-identifiable
effluvia. Fishmongers exhort the crowds with carny-like shouts, each
extolling the freshness and superiority of their particular wares. The
occasional prostitute wanders through, on their way to providing the
services of Andolor's oldest profession to the dock crowd.
 
  Fellchantry's docks lie to the west, offering an escape from the square.
Farther east an unusually lively building boasts signs claiming the coldest
beer in the Barony.

<MAPEND>
[ Exits: north east south west ]
A man moves about the crowd, trying to peddle fish to shocked onlookers.
A man in a guard's uniform walks here, no doubt a justiciary.

The Heart of the Mystery
  Alas, some foul tragedy seems to have occurred here, for nothing else
could so reliably draw such a diverse crowd of onlookers. Loud cries of
"Murder most foul!" and "What villainy!" abound. At the center of the
whole mess, mayhap literally as well as figuratively, stand a group of His
Majesty's Justiciars observing one very dead body. The darkness of the
deed and the storm of intrigue sure to follow are a fitting complement to
the dark and stormy nights so common in the Barony.

  Fellchantry Square stretches out in all directions, oblivious to the
fact that Death has paid a visit nearby.

Fellchantry Square
  For all Fellchantry's Square's boasting of a dense population, here the 
moving and close press of bodies is less apparent. Sparser, in fact, the 
closer one moves towards the hulking drawbridge which lies eastwards and is 
stationed with men in glimmering armor and pointy weapons of all varieties 
and levels of use. Beyond the bridge and an impressive distance into the sky 
stretches a fort, littered with arrow slits and even more pointy materials 
leveled towards the grounds below.
 
To the north, south and west, the Square continues to sprawl out and avail 
itself of the free (yet more dangerous) space offered here.

Bridge Three
  A tale as old as time, the denizens of Fellchantry have wondered for many 
decades - perhaps centuries - why the very structure which bridges 
Fellchantry Square and the dwelling of His Lordship, Lord Whatshisface, had 
never gotten an official name. Lo, the name of this bridge is carved into the
timbers as well as the burly men who stand watch upon it; their arms are like
tree stumps and their stances that of great sentries who guard the good 
Lord's halls. Lo, they nor their impassive watch comes to a halt.

Justiciar Headquarters
  This aged building, remarkable only in that it's slightly less run down than
the structures around it, is home to His Majesty's Justiciars. From here
Fellchantry's city guards work hard at the appearance of upholding justice.
In reality the guards are only about two steps removed from being criminals
themselves, and the sour reek of tobacco, alcohol, and sweat on the air says
much about the Justiciars' efficacy. Still, the Baron's coat of arms hangs
large on the wall, and that's all the legitimacy these men need.

  His Majesty's Kangaroo Court is in the western wing of the courthouse. To
the south wait the pickpockets and cutpurses of Fellchantry Square.

His Majesty's Court of Justice
    A large dais at the westernmost end of a long walkway is the most prominent
feature of His Majesty's Court of Justice. On it is a simple judge's bench,
its face decorated with the Baron's coat of arms. Those wondering about the
Baron's views on justice can find their questions answered by the large
painting that totally dominates the wall behind the bench. Simply titled,
"Justice," it depicts a woman with a radiant halo and pure white vestments
holding a sword aloft with one elegantly-sandled foot atop a pile of corpses.
It's not exactly the sort of court at whose mercy one throws oneself.
Non-descript hardwood benches are arranged in two aisles so that the
populace may observe the proceedings of the court, though few ever do.
 
  The way back east leads to the Justiciar Headquarters, and to the bustling
city square beyond.

Some minutes pass while those few interested in the case settle down in their seats for the hearing.

Justiciar Amara ju Nulaha asks, "Jonah Nessim, you stand trial here,
 today, on charges of murder and theft- the appropriation of the Founder's
 jeweled egg.  How do you plead?"

Jonah Nessim says, "Lady Justiciar, I plead innocence, for I had not--"
The woman at the bench interrupts him.

Justiciar Amara ju Nulaha says, "Unnamed testimonies proclaim you had been
 in pursuit of Juilus Sannar at the time, and once you tumbled to the
 cobbles, the victim was found bleeding."

Jonah Nessim says, "Lady Justiciar, I was unarmed."

Justiciar Amara ju Nulaha asks, "Indeed, you were at the time, though you
 needn't have been.  Juilus was dispossessed of his dirk.  Where had you
 hidden the weapon?"

Detective Bane Jones says, "Lady Justiciar, if I may interject."

Justiciar Amara ju Nulaha permits the interruption with a nod, though her mouth tightens.

Detective Bane Jones says, "I had scoured Fellchantry, meticulously - and
 quite brilliantly, if I may add - received several testimonies from
 notable townsfolk on the actual occurences on that day."
Detective Bane Jones says, "If you would permit this submission of
 evidence?  All have been signed as true."

Justiciar Amara ju Nulaha says, "Very well, but first.  Jonah Nessim,
 recount the events of the day, lest we eliminate the possibility of
 contradiction."

A bead of sweat forms upon Jonah's brow.

Jonah Nessim says, "We had been pursued by a vile savage, Lady Justiciar,
 no doubt their attempt at procuring the egg for themselves.  We could not
 determine whether it was a man or a woman."
Jonah Nessim says, "What I do recall of their visage, they were cloaked in
 brown with a red heart embroidered at the forehead of the hood."

Jonah Nessim says, "After a brief struggle, we set off and were pursued. 
 We had reached Fellchantry square, though I was sent crown over petticoats
 and crashed into the cobbles below."

Jonah Nessim says, "Alas, once I found my feet, we were left sans pursuer,
 and sans the jeweled egg."

Justiciar Amara ju Nulaha says, "The Fellchantry Heart are a children's
 tale, Jonah.  You'd have earned yourself more credibility if not for such
 a ridiculous detail."

Jonah Nessim says, "But, Lady Justiciar--"

Justiciar Amara ju Nulaha says, "Silence!  I have been inundated with
 enough such poppycock."

Detective Bane Jones says, "Lady Justiciar, among these testimonies is one
 signed by Baron Kormack himself.  It may behoove you to give it a
 gander."
Detective Bane Jones walks over to the Justiciar and hands over the sheaf of notes.
The Lady Justiciar glances over the sheaf and lets out a resigned shrug.

Justiciar Amara ju Nulaha says, "I grant you this, then, Detective.  You
 have three days to find this phantom killer of yours.  If none turn up,
 then Jonah Nessim will be sentenced to drawing and quartering.  I am sure
 you understand why."

The detective nods and turns to you.
Detective Bane Jones says, "You know what to do, KumoGami."

 cells."

Oberon Nook

park tucked away in a forgotten corner of the barony. The grasses which roll 
across the area are maintained with care, the sparse scattering of trees also
adding to the charm of this 'clearing' between buildings. Several benches are
featured, at least one occupied at all times while children entertain 
themselves in the open space under the supervision of the eternal gloomy sky 
overhead.

Eastwards, one may travel back to the vibrant Oberon Alley.

<MAPEND>
[ Exits: east ]
(Golden Aura) A man in a cloak with red heart embroidered on its forehead stalks the alleyways.
(Red Aura) A member of the Guild walks the alleys, perusing the available wares.
(Red Aura) Peddling his wares, this man waves you over.
How odd, you could have sworn that the brown-cloaked man was here just a moment ago...

Medical lounge (G)
  You stand in a plain looking room, with bunk beds lining both sides. Green 
wool blankets line the beds with perfect hospital corners. At the end of this 
seemingly endless room are two doors leading to what you believe is some 
kind of latrine and shower area. On one wall there is a milk cooler next to a 
sign that shows a Drill Sergeant pointing to the room. Words are written 
over his head, "Milk makes for a strong soldier!". There is a Second 
Lieutenant Pixie with a red cross on her hat here.

Boot Camp Headquarters (G)
  As you enter the Boot Camp Headquarters, you immediately notice that
the large main hall is adorned with feasting tables and fire pits
allowing the green recruits to relax after a hard days training.
A large mural on the northern wall depicts the founding members of the
Boot Camp standing before The Fallen Soldier on an ancient battlefield.
The other stone walls are decorated in the green and yellow insignia of
Boot Camp and various 'Boot Needs You' posters depicting an alluring Diva
dressed in the Boot Camp colours pointing at you.
From the arches leading out of the hall drift sounds of young recruits
being put through their paces and the smells of gunpowder and mud linger
in the air.

The Grand City of Aylor (G)
  You stand on the edge of the beautiful City of Aylor.
 
A bright light shines down from the heavens, pouring over you, bathing you
in its warm glow.  Everything around you seems rich and pure in color.  An
enormous, white temple stands to the north, taking up most of your view.
 
To reach the Aylorian Academy, you must travel up the large staircase that
stands just off the side of the church.  (Type 'UP' to learn how to play the
game.)
 
Below you are large piles of armor and equipment discarded by other
adventurers.

Crumbling Field
  This field is slowly crumbling into the rushing river to the east. As you 
watch, more and more of the unprotected shoreline ripples away into the 
thunderous water. To the northwest, a small forest broods over the fields all
around it. Somewhere eastwards, a small trail collapses into what has become 
known as Kettermoor Crick: the fishy river leading into what is known as 
Mesolar's melting pot of debauchery. One may merely cross the Kettermoor to 
enter Fellchantry.

On the Crickbridge Road
  It was a dark and stormy night...

  There's a saying out in the darker parts of the country that, for a man
in the right kinds of trouble, all roads lead to Fellchantry. They say that
when "No Fear" Narlfryd, the famed Wolfen daredevil, needed a place to lay
low, he came to Fellchantry and knifed a guy over a card game. The story
goes that he wanted to use a vacation in a cell as a chance to let a bad
storm blow over. The authorities didn't give him the chance. They took one
look at that body, shook their heads, and walked the other way. Fellchantry
is just that kind of place. Around here, they're ALL dark and stormy nights,
and the residents like it that way just fine.

  To the east lies the bridge over Kettermoor Crick, the deceptively named
fast-running river that supplies Fellchantry with its ne'erending supply of
fish, trade taxes, and surly attitudes.

<MAPEND>

Oberon Alley (1285)

Oberon Nook
  The alleyways eventually open up into Oberon Nook, very much resembling a 
park tucked away in a forgotten corner of the barony. The grasses which roll 
across the area are maintained with care, the sparse scattering of trees also
adding to the charm of this 'clearing' between buildings. Several benches are
featured, at least one occupied at all times while children entertain 
themselves in the open space under the supervision of the eternal gloomy sky 
overhead.

Eastwards, one may travel back to the vibrant Oberon Alley.

Dead End in Bottlebreak Alley [**> PK <**]
  This particular pathway comes to an end here. The alley leads up to an 
unoccupied square with most buildings facing away from the alley itself, 
though the odd back door may be spied where servants or tenants would empty 
their chamberpots out onto the cobble underfoot. Wheels with wire along their
edges are mounted from east to west, top-floor tenants pinning and rolling 
(rare) laundry out to dry. Some of those textiles still drip beneath the 
eternal gloom of Fellchantry.

s
Bottlebreak Alley [**> PK <**]
  The smells wafting through this alley are less charming than those elsewhere 
within the Barony, but not bad enough for one to run for the hills. Folk who 
traffic here tend to always have a bottle tucked beneath an arm, however, as 
they move from one seedy tavern to another, eyeing anyone who they may not 
recognize suspiciously. Words can be had about the general odour of unwashed 
bodies, however. The state of the surrounding buildings does not suggest 
dilapidation to the point where its denizens should look and smell the way 
they do, though the feeling of complacency hangs thick in the air.

<MAPEND>

w
Murder Alley
  A bit of a narrower path between buildings, this area does not seem to 
receive a lot of traffic. The buildings which flank the road to the north and
south are a bit more ramshackle, the air feels a bit colder, and the ground 
is a bit grimier. Upon closer inspection of the northern building, one may 
notice the trademark giving this passage its name. A splash of dark paint 
(someone dropped a bucket, no doubt) smears across the wall, the impact 
having left many spots, giving one the illusion that a throat was cut.

<MAPEND>

Treadway Alley
  The pleasantries seemingly associated with Treadway Alley continue here, some

themselves here reading the new gossip prints of the week over a drink or 
warm beverage and a warm pastry produced from an adjecent bakery. It is clear
that if one were to look for folk with fewer scruples, a journey deeper into 
the network of alleyways may be in order.

A bend in the path leads eastwards, one's northern and western flanks blocked
off by buildings.

Treadway Alley
  A rather open space for an alley, a multitude of tables and chairs are 
scattered around the area, serving as a quaint space for an outdoor drink or 
smoke among the regulars in this area. Some of the doors against the eastern 
buildings lead towards shops, some to homes, and others to homes with their 
back rooms converted into shops, all selling a series of curious wares of 
varying value. The cobblestones underfoot appear to be dark and glisten 
always, as if moistened under the toil of recent rains despite the 
ever-present overhead gloom.

The alleyway continues to the north and south, westwards lies Bogboil Bridge.

w
Bogboil Bridge
  Some may call it a bridge, others may call it a hack, but the fact that it 
allows people to cross water is one set in stone. A multitude of planks run 
from one end of the stone pavement across a narrow river from the western to 
the eastern side. The tightly-packed buildings receive a bit of a gap here, 
though one may spy that a few brave souls have taken it upon themselves to 
construct ramshackle balconies in order to appreciate their 'ocean view'.
Eastwards, the alleyways split at an intersection and vanish beyond sight.

Brimtoil Alley
  Past the northern bustle one comes to the calmer, plainer and saner
environment of Fellchantry's alleyways. There are still the odd buildings 
with awkward doors upon surprisingly sturdy hinges from which men and women 
conduct their many creative business ventures, though they are sparser, the 
people here skinnier and rattier, their eyes sharper, and their weapons 
always at hand. A sharp curve eventually leads across a small bridge to the 
east, eventually plunging even deeper into the (known) underbelly of the 
barony.

Brimtoil Alley
  The entrance to the small network of Fellchantry's alleyways seems to be more
populated than further in. Establishments, all of clean and honorable repute 
of course, have taken down walls and built doors, setting up tables or stalls
along the eastern and western side, trading in weapons, oddly valuable 
jewelry, gems, glass passed off as gems, illusions passed off as glass, and 
lies passed off as illusions. Upon close inspection, one may even spy one of 
the Justiciary among the patrons of this fine market road.

Further south, the alleyway eventually twists east and out of sight.

n
Fellchantry Square
  A very curious amount of folks who traffic to the south have their hoods 
drawn, save the braver and more scary-looking individuals who stalk with the 
deadly (and frankly, sometimes swaying) grace of the land's most hardened 
criminals, traffickers and scorned illegitimate children ever to be produced
on Andolorian soil. It's not difficult to suss out the fact that in yonder 
direction lies a network of alleyways, nor is it difficult to determine that 
some folks are simply not welcome among the raff. Nay, quite often an unlucky
individual would find themselves pleading, hoisted by their britches and 
tossed from the narrow building flanks into the pounded cobble below, ejected
from the seedy underbelly of Fellchantry.

<MAPEND>

w
Fellchantry Square
  For all Fellchantry's Square's boasting of a dense population, here the 
moving and close press of bodies is less apparent. Sparser, in fact, the 
closer one moves towards the hulking drawbridge which lies eastwards and is 
stationed with men in glimmering armor and pointy weapons of all varieties 
and levels of use. Beyond the bridge and an impressive distance into the sky 
stretches a fort, littered with arrow slits and even more pointy materials 
leveled towards the grounds below.
 
To the north, south and west, the Square continues to sprawl out and avail 
itself of the free (yet more dangerous) space offered here.

>>
The Heart of the Mystery
  Alas, some foul tragedy seems to have occurred here, for nothing else
could so reliably draw such a diverse crowd of onlookers. Loud cries of
"Murder most foul!" and "What villainy!" abound. At the center of the
whole mess, mayhap literally as well as figuratively, stand a group of His
Majesty's Justiciars observing one very dead body. The darkness of the
deed and the storm of intrigue sure to follow are a fitting complement to
the dark and stormy nights so common in the Barony.

  Fellchantry Square stretches out in all directions, oblivious to the
fact that Death has paid a visit nearby.

n
Fellchantry Square [**> PK <**]
    The signature smell of Fellchantry (jokingly referred to as "Kettermoor
Cologne") wafts in with particular potency from the west, hinting at
the docks to be found in that direction. The aroma, not so much unpleasant
as it is unusual, has strong fishy accents punctuated with less-identifiable
effluvia. Fishmongers exhort the crowds with carny-like shouts, each
extolling the freshness and superiority of their particular wares. The
occasional prostitute wanders through, on their way to providing the
services of Andolor's oldest profession to the dock crowd.
 
  Fellchantry's docks lie to the west, offering an escape from the square.
Farther east an unusually lively building boasts signs claiming the coldest
beer in the Barony.

w
Fellchantry Square
  The presence of the barony's courthouse to the north does nothing to curb
the traffic of the usual ne'er-do-wells and cutthroats here. For the majority
of the Justiciars-- Fellchantry's city guards-- the pay just isn't good
enough to really make an effort. The occasional drunk gets roughed up, and
a murderer may even be arrested if he's a little too indiscrete, but in the
end it's just keeping up appearances. Who cares about a murder when no one
misses the deceased? Besides, everyone in Fellchantry is guilty of something.

  Justice waits to the north, longing for someone to avenge the slander done
to her name. The square looms predatorily to the east and south.

n
Justiciar Headquarters
  This aged building, remarkable only in that it's slightly less run down than
the structures around it, is home to His Majesty's Justiciars. From here
Fellchantry's city guards work hard at the appearance of upholding justice.
In reality the guards are only about two steps removed from being criminals
themselves, and the sour reek of tobacco, alcohol, and sweat on the air says
much about the Justiciars' efficacy. Still, the Baron's coat of arms hangs
large on the wall, and that's all the legitimacy these men need.

  His Majesty's Kangaroo Court is in the western wing of the courthouse. To
the south wait the pickpockets and cutpurses of Fellchantry Square.

e
Fellchantry Square
  Here, filled with all manner of sights and smells, is Fellchantry Square.
In the constant hell of the Barony, this is where the honest (and you have
to be flexible on your definition here) citizens come to gossip, barter, and
conduct their necessary business. The square is a microcosm of the city; all
cramped buildings, bustling crowds, and narrow side streets. A guy could get
lost with the slightest wandering from the beaten path, and he probably
wouldn't like where he ended up. The only thing less welcoming than
Fellchantry's main streets are its back alleys.
 
  The spikes of the raised Kettermoor gate loom to the west like a dragon
waiting for a snack. From all other directions the cramped chaos of the
square presses in.

Bridge Three
  A tale as old as time, the denizens of Fellchantry have wondered for many 
decades - perhaps centuries - why the very structure which bridges 
Fellchantry Square and the dwelling of His Lordship, Lord Whatshisface, had 
never gotten an official name. Lo, the name of this bridge is carved into the
timbers as well as the burly men who stand watch upon it; their arms are like
tree stumps and their stances that of great sentries who guard the good 
Lord's halls. Lo, they nor their impassive watch comes to a halt.
  
Lo, how snugly their britches fit.

Elroy Castle Entrance Hall
  How grand an entrance hall you find yourself within - serving wenches in nary
a linen and fine gentlemen wearing but scraps of silk - one would find 
themselves hard-pressed to be within such luxury if not for the subtle signs 
of cracks within the walls and ominous copper-like stains within the ceiling.
Alas, the marbled floors are home to great statues of even more marble and 
cheaper materials, no doubt having been harvested from proprietors who also 
produced the tasteless glass-shrouded chandeliers overhead.

Fellchantry Square
  For all Fellchantry's Square's boasting of a dense population, here the 
moving and close press of bodies is less apparent. Sparser, in fact, the 
closer one moves towards the hulking drawbridge which lies eastwards and is 
stationed with men in glimmering armor and pointy weapons of all varieties 
and levels of use. Beyond the bridge and an impressive distance into the sky 
stretches a fort, littered with arrow slits and even more pointy materials 
leveled towards the grounds below.
 
To the north, south and west, the Square continues to sprawl out and avail 
itself of the free (yet more dangerous) space offered here.

The Heart of the Mystery
  Alas, some foul tragedy seems to have occurred here, for nothing else
could so reliably draw such a diverse crowd of onlookers. Loud cries of

deed and the storm of intrigue sure to follow are a fitting complement to
the dark and stormy nights so common in the Barony.

Brimtoil Alley
  The entrance to the small network of Fellchantry's alleyways seems to be more
populated than further in. Establishments, all of clean and honorable repute 
of course, have taken down walls and built doors, setting up tables or stalls
along the eastern and western side, trading in weapons, oddly valuable 
jewelry, gems, glass passed off as gems, illusions passed off as glass, and 
lies passed off as illusions. Upon close inspection, one may even spy one of 
the Justiciary among the patrons of this fine market road.

n
Fellchantry Square
  Most of the traffic at this intersection of the square is either coming
from or going toward the south. The third most corrupt organization in the
city (after its government, and its law enforcement) has its guild hall in
that direction, and with the recent trade talks announced by the Baron there
are plenty of foreigners and citizens alike who feel the need to visit the
Merchant's Guild. Hatred and bigotry wash from Fellchantry's citizens in a
palpable wave toward the outlanders with their strange features, strange
clothing, and strange ways. Likewise in a southerly direction are the homes
of some of Fellchantry's more affluent, non-royal citizens, as well as
several other guild halls. There is even said to be an assassin's guild,
but who can afford to believe everything they hear?
   
  Affluence is to the south, along with all the dark deeds it can buy. The
press of stinking bodies in the square is all around.

to be flexible on your definition here) citizens come to gossip, barter, and

2968/5230 HP  4623/5687 MP  1306/1322 mv  740tnl  
Lv 168  G 150176 | Fellchantry Square (NESW)
>>
w
The Bridge Over Kettermoor Crick
    The rushing waters of Kettermoor Crick flow far below this sturdy stone
bridge. In the miserable old days, the people that first settled this
godsforsaken scar of land built the bridge to access Fellchantry-- the squat,
sprawling island that sits astride the river like the biggest bully in the
schoolyard. Or so they say anyway... Really, it'd make just as much sense if
they built the bridge to give themselves something high enough to jump from.
Fellchantry isn't what you'd call a vacation spot. The water is colder
and darker than a witch's heart. The fog-- like a mourner's veil-- stretches
perpetually over the land, as if the sun just can't eat a big enough
breakfast to ever cook it off. This is where dreams go to die.

  To the west the Crickbridge Road leads away from town. To the east the city
of Fellchantry looms, looking like the saddest verse of the most dismal dirge
you've ever heard. If the word on the street is true, then the murdered smith
is somewhere inside, his body giving off the putrescent stench of a mystery.

<MAPEND>

w
On the Crickbridge Road
  It was a dark and stormy night...

  There's a saying out in the darker parts of the country that, for a man
in the right kinds of trouble, all roads lead to Fellchantry. They say that
when "No Fear" Narlfryd, the famed Wolfen daredevil, needed a place to lay
low, he came to Fellchantry and knifed a guy over a card game. The story
goes that he wanted to use a vacation in a cell as a chance to let a bad
storm blow over. The authorities didn't give him the chance. They took one
look at that body, shook their heads, and walked the other way. Fellchantry
is just that kind of place. Around here, they're ALL dark and stormy nights,
and the residents like it that way just fine.

  To the east lies the bridge over Kettermoor Crick, the deceptively named
fast-running river that supplies Fellchantry with its ne'erending supply of
fish, trade taxes, and surly attitudes.

<MAPEND>
[ Exits: east west ]

help fly
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Help Keywords : Fly Land.
Help Category : Enhancement.
Related Helps : Levitation.
Last Updated  : 2017-08-28 10:03:56.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------

Syntax: cast 'fly' <character>
Spell Number: 48

With only the force of his will, the caster can rise into the air and
soar with the eagles.  A character that is flying does not need a boat
to cross deep water, and will not be hindered by quicksand.

Races that have the ability to fly naturally can type 'fly' and 'land'
at any time outside combat. The ability to use 'land' to cancel a fly effect
is not available to others.

Potions of flight are also available at various stores throughout Andolor,
including Aeleron's Alchemy supplies in Aylor.

Primary stat: Intelligence.
Affected by : None.


----------------------------------------------------------------------------

Medical lounge (G)
  You stand in a plain looking room, with bunk beds lining both sides. Green 
wool blankets line the beds with perfect hospital corners. At the end of this 
seemingly endless room are two doors leading to what you believe is some 
kind of latrine and shower area. On one wall there is a milk cooler next to a 
sign that shows a Drill Sergeant pointing to the room. Words are written 
over his head, "Milk makes for a strong soldier!". There is a Second 
Lieutenant Pixie with a red cross on her hat here.

Boot Camp Headquarters (G)
  As you enter the Boot Camp Headquarters, you immediately notice that
the large main hall is adorned with feasting tables and fire pits
allowing the green recruits to relax after a hard days training.
A large mural on the northern wall depicts the founding members of the
Boot Camp standing before The Fallen Soldier on an ancient battlefield.
The other stone walls are decorated in the green and yellow insignia of
Boot Camp and various 'Boot Needs You' posters depicting an alluring Diva
dressed in the Boot Camp colours pointing at you.
From the arches leading out of the hall drift sounds of young recruits
being put through their paces and the smells of gunpowder and mud linger
in the air.

The Grand City of Aylor (G)
  You stand on the edge of the beautiful City of Aylor.
 
A bright light shines down from the heavens, pouring over you, bathing you
in its warm glow.  Everything around you seems rich and pure in color.  An
enormous, white temple stands to the north, taking up most of your view.
 
To reach the Aylorian Academy, you must travel up the large staircase that
stands just off the side of the church.  (Type 'UP' to learn how to play the
game.)
 
Below you are large piles of armor and equipment discarded by other
adventurers.

Boot Camp Headquarters (G)
  As you enter the Boot Camp Headquarters, you immediately notice that
the large main hall is adorned with feasting tables and fire pits
allowing the green recruits to relax after a hard days training.
A large mural on the northern wall depicts the founding members of the
Boot Camp standing before The Fallen Soldier on an ancient battlefield.
The other stone walls are decorated in the green and yellow insignia of
Boot Camp and various 'Boot Needs You' posters depicting an alluring Diva
dressed in the Boot Camp colours pointing at you.
From the arches leading out of the hall drift sounds of young recruits
being put through their paces and the smells of gunpowder and mud linger
in the air.

Recreation Room (G)
  Walking into the room, you notice there is a relaxed, friendly atmosphere and
almost everyone is in military uniform. A jukebox is playing a lively tune

Boot Camp Headquarters (G)
  As you enter the Boot Camp Headquarters, you immediately notice that
the large main hall is adorned with feasting tables and fire pits
allowing the green recruits to relax after a hard days training.
A large mural on the northern wall depicts the founding members of the
Boot Camp standing before The Fallen Soldier on an ancient battlefield.
The other stone walls are decorated in the green and yellow insignia of
Boot Camp and various 'Boot Needs You' posters depicting an alluring Diva
dressed in the Boot Camp colours pointing at you.
From the arches leading out of the hall drift sounds of young recruits
being put through their paces and the smells of gunpowder and mud linger
in the air.

The Grand City of Aylor (G)
  You stand on the edge of the beautiful City of Aylor.

in its warm glow.  Everything around you seems rich and pure in color.  An
enormous, white temple stands to the north, taking up most of your view.

stands just off the side of the church.  (Type 'UP' to learn how to play the

adventurers.

making mystic gestures and chanting in an ancient and near-forgotten tongue.  She

against the wall.  When the air clears and you can see again, a small crystal bottle

You give a small crystal bottle to the King Elbryan.
The King Elbryan asks, "Ah!  This is from Allora, you say?  Could it be,
 after all these years, she finally forgives me?"
The King Elbryan sighs.
The King Elbryan says, "I have spent so many years thinking of what I
 could do differently.  Alas, Allora was lost to us all by then.  My
 beloved Beth has been a treasure, and I love her as dearly as I loved
 Allora."
Elbryan smiles mistily.
The King Elbryan says, "I will drink this in her memory, and pray she one
 day returns to us."
Elbryan raises the crystal bottle and drinks the potion.  A thunderclap
sounds in the room as he falls to the floor, clutching his stomach.
A bright flash of light blinds everyone for a moment, and when your
vision clears, Allora is standing over the writhing form of the King
Elbryan, laughing madly.  Her black, glittering eyes remind you of a
spider's dispassionate gaze, and she is dressed in black cobwebs and
spidersilk.
Allora screams in fury when she sees you standing over Elbryan's
fallen body.
Allora the Black exclaims, "Traitor!  You have killed my love!  Elbryan! 
 Elbryan, my beloved!"

Allora the Black is in perfect health.
